<pr_description>
Flag mixing up "flaunt" and "flout"
**"Flaunt"** means to show off / be ostentatious. **"Flout"** means to openly ignore rules.

This doesn't seem to be common on GitHub but on the wider internet "flaunt" is a very common mistake where "flout" is obviously meant. (The reverse is nowhere near as common.)

- He **flaunted** US bankruptcy laws for personal gain.
- It's got a Kirk-esque captain who **flaunts** the rules in favour of 'getting her done' and who is fiercely loyal to his people.
- That's what deranged scientists **flaunting** the laws of God and Man are for
- While a lot of users have genuine trouble writing questions up in English, some seem to **flaunt** the basic rules of punctuation and grammar.

</pr_description>

    25	                            None$(.or(Some($lint_kind)))?,
    26	                        ),
    27	                    ),
    28	                );
    29	            )+
    30	        };
    31	    }
    32	
    33	    // Each correction pair has multiple bad forms and multiple correct forms.
    34	    macro_rules! add_many_to_many_mappings {
    35	        ($group:expr, {
    36	            $($name:expr => ($input_correction_multi_pairs:expr, $message:expr, $description:expr $(, $lint_kind:expr)?)),+ $(,)?
    37	        }) => {
    38	            $(
    39	                $group.add_chunk_expr_linter(
    40	                    $name,
    41	                    Box::new(
    42	                        MapPhraseSetLinter::many_to_many(
    43	                            $input_correction_multi_pairs,
    44	                            $message,
    45	                            $description,
    46	                            None$(.or(Some($lint_kind)))?,
    47	                        ),
    48	                    ),
    49	                );
    50	            )+
    51	        };
    52	    }
    53

     1	use super::{ExprLinter, Lint, LintKind};
     2	use crate::CharStringExt;
     3	use crate::expr::Expr;
     4	use crate::expr::FixedPhrase;
     5	use crate::expr::LongestMatchOf;
     6	use crate::linting::Suggestion;
     7	use crate::linting::expr_linter::Chunk;
     8	use crate::{Token, TokenStringExt};
     9	
    10	pub struct MapPhraseSetLinter<'a> {
    11	    description: String,
    12	    expr: LongestMatchOf,
    13	    wrong_forms_to_correct_forms: &'a [(&'a str, &'a str)],
    14	    multi_wrong_forms_to_multi_correct_forms: &'a [(&'a [&'a str], &'a [&'a str])],
    15	    message: String,
    16	    lint_kind: LintKind,
    17	}
    18	
    19	impl<'a> MapPhraseSetLinter<'a> {
    20	    pub fn one_to_one(
    21	        wrong_forms_to_correct_forms: &'a [(&'a str, &'a str)],
    22	        message: impl ToString,
    23	        description: impl ToString,
    24	        lint_kind: Option<LintKind>,
    25	    ) -> Self {
    26	        let expr = LongestMatchOf::new(
    27	            wrong_forms_to_correct_forms
    28	                .iter()
    29	                .map(|(wrong_form, _correct_form)| {
    30	                    let expr: Box<dyn Expr> = Box::new(FixedPhrase::from_phrase(wrong_form));
    31	                    expr
    32	                })
    33	                .collect(),
    34	        );
    35	
    36	        Self {
    37	            description: description.to_string(),
    38	            expr,
    39	            wrong_forms_to_correct_forms,
    40	            multi_wrong_forms_to_multi_correct_forms: &[],
    41	            message: message.to_string(),
    42	            lint_kind: lint_kind.unwrap_or(LintKind::Miscellaneous),
    43	        }
    44	    }
    45	
    46	    pub fn many_to_many(
    47	        multi_wrong_forms_to_multi_correct_forms: &'a [(&'a [&'a str], &'a [&'a str])],
    48	        message: impl ToString,
    49	        description: impl ToString,
    50	        lint_kind: Option<LintKind>,
    51	    ) -> Self {
    52	        let mut lmo = LongestMatchOf::new(Vec::new());
    53	        for (wrong_forms, _correct_forms) in multi_wrong_forms_to_multi_correct_forms {
    54	            for wrong_form in wrong_forms.iter() {
    55	                lmo.add(FixedPhrase::from_phrase(wrong_form));
    56	            }
    57	        }
    58	        let expr = lmo;
    59	
    60	        Self {
    61	            description: description.to_string(),
    62	            expr,
    63	            wrong_forms_to_correct_forms: &[],
    64	            multi_wrong_forms_to_multi_correct_forms,
    65	            message: message.to_string(),
    66	            lint_kind: lint_kind.unwrap_or(LintKind::Miscellaneous),
    67	        }
    68	    }
    69	}
    70	
    71	impl<'a> ExprLinter for MapPhraseSetLinter<'a> {
    72	    type Unit = Chunk;
    73	
    74	    fn expr(&self) -> &dyn Expr {
    75	        &self.expr
    76	    }
    77	
    78	    fn match_to_lint(&self, matched_tokens: &[Token], source: &[char]) -> Option<Lint> {
    79	        let span = matched_tokens.span()?;
    80	        let matched_text = span.get_content(source);
    81	
    82	        let mut suggestions: Vec<_> = self
    83	            .wrong_forms_to_correct_forms
    84	            .iter()
    85	            .filter(|(wrong_form, _)| matched_text.eq_ignore_ascii_case_str(wrong_form))
    86	            .map(|(_, correct_form)| {
    87	                Suggestion::replace_with_match_case(correct_form.chars().collect(), matched_text)
    88	            })
    89	            .collect();
    90	
    91	        let many_to_many_suggestions: Vec<_> = self
    92	            .multi_wrong_forms_to_multi_correct_forms
    93	            .iter()
    94	            .flat_map(|(wrong_forms, correct_forms)| {
    95	                wrong_forms
    96	                    .iter()
    97	                    .filter(move |&&wrong_form| matched_text.eq_ignore_ascii_case_str(wrong_form))
    98	                    .flat_map(move |_| {
    99	                        correct_forms.iter().map(move |correct_form| {
   100	                            Suggestion::replace_with_match_case(
   101	                                correct_form.chars().collect(),
   102	                                matched_text,
   103	                            )
   104	                        })
   105	                    })
   106	            })
   107	            .collect();
   108	
   109	        suggestions.extend(many_to_many_suggestions);
   110	
   111	        if suggestions.is_empty() {
   112	            return None;
   113	        }
   114	
   115	        Some(Lint {
   116	            span,
   117	            lint_kind: self.lint_kind,
   118	            suggestions,
   119	            message: self.message.to_string(),
   120	            priority: 31,
   121	        })
   122	    }
   123	
   124	    fn description(&self) -> &str {
   125	        self.description.as_str()
   126	    }
   127	}
   128

   130	    fn match_to_lint(&self, toks: &[Token], src: &[char]) -> Option<Lint> {
   131	        // Helper functions make the match tables more compact and readable.
   132	        let norm = |i: usize| toks[i].span.get_content_string(src).to_lowercase();
   133	        let isws = |i: usize| toks[i].kind.is_whitespace();
   134	        let tokspan = |i: usize| toks[i].span;
   135	        let slicespan = |i: usize| toks[i..i + 3].span().unwrap();
   136	
   137	        let (span, replacement, pos) = match toks.len() {
   138	            2 => match (norm(0).as_str(), norm(1).as_str()) {
   139	                ("everyday", _) => Some((tokspan(0), "every day", "adverb")),
   140	                _ => None,
   141	            },
   142	            3 => match (norm(0).as_str(), norm(2).as_str()) {
   143	                ("everyday", _) if isws(1) => Some((tokspan(0), "every day", "adverb")),
   144	                (_, "everyday") if isws(1) => Some((tokspan(2), "every day", "adverb")),
   145	                _ => None,
   146	            },
   147	            5 => match (norm(0).as_str(), norm(2).as_str(), norm(4).as_str()) {
   148	                ("every", "day", _) if isws(1) && isws(3) => {
   149	                    Some((slicespan(0), "everyday", "adjective"))
   150	                }
   151	                (_, "every", "day") if isws(1) && isws(3) => {
   152	                    Some((slicespan(2), "everyday", "adjective"))
   153	                }
   154	                ("everyday", _, _) if isws(1) && isws(3) => {
   155	                    Some((tokspan(0), "every day", "adverb"))
   156	                }
   157	                _ => None,
   158	            },
   159	            6 => match (
   160	                norm(0).as_str(),
   161	                norm(2).as_str(),
   162	                norm(4).as_str(),
   163	                norm(5).as_str(),
   164	            ) {
   165	                ("every", "day", _, _) if isws(1) && isws(3) => {
   166	                    Some((slicespan(0), "everyday", "adjective"))
   167	                }
   168	                _ => None,
   169	            },
   170	            _ => None,
   171	        }?;
   172	
   173	        Some(Lint {
   174	            span,
   175	            lint_kind: LintKind::WordChoice,
   176	            suggestions: vec![Suggestion::replace_with_match_case_str(
   177	                replacement,
   178	                span.get_content(src),
   179	            )],
   180	            message: format!("You probably mean the {pos} `{replacement}` here."),
   181	            priority: 31,
   182	        })
   183	    }
   184

   186	        "This rule tries to sort out confusing the adjective `everyday` and the adverb `every day`."
   187	    }
   188	}

   265	use crate::{Document, LSend, render_markdown};
   266	
   267	/// A __stateless__ rule that searches documents for grammatical errors.
   268	///
   269	/// Commonly implemented via [`ExprLinter`].
   270	///
   271	/// See also: [`LintGroup`].
   272	pub trait Linter: LSend {
   273	    /// Analyzes a document and produces zero or more [`Lint`]s.
   274	    /// We pass `self` mutably for caching purposes.
   275	    fn lint(&mut self, document: &Document) -> Vec<Lint>;
   276	    /// A user-facing description of what kinds of grammatical errors this rule looks for.
   277	    /// It is usually shown in settings menus.
   278	    fn description(&self) -> &str;
   279	}
   280	
   281	/// A blanket-implemented trait that renders the Markdown description field of a linter to HTML.
   282	pub trait HtmlDescriptionLinter {
   283	    fn description_html(&self) -> String;
   284	}
   285	
   286	impl<L: ?Sized> HtmlDescriptionLinter for L
   287	where
   288	    L: Linter,
   289	{
   290	    fn description_html(&self) -> String {
   291	        let desc = self.description();
   292	        render_markdown(desc)
   293	    }
   294	}
   295	
   296	pub mod debug {
   297	    use crate::Token;
   298	
   299	    /// Formats a lint match with surrounding context for debug output.
   300	    ///
   301	    /// The function takes the same `matched_tokens` and `source`, and `context` parameters
   302	    /// passed to `[match_to_lint_with_context]`.
   303	    ///
   304	    /// # Arguments
   305	    /// * `log` - `matched_tokens`
   306	    /// * `ctx` - `context`, or `None` if calling from `[match_to_lint]`
   307	    /// * `src` - `source` from `[match_to_lint]` / `[match_to_lint_with_context]`
   308	    ///
   309	    /// # Returns
   310	    /// A string with ANSI escape codes where:
   311	    /// - Context tokens are dimmed before and after the matched tokens in normal weight.
   312	    /// - Markup and formatting text hidden in whitespace tokens is filtered out.
   313	    pub fn format_lint_match(
   314	        log: &[Token],
   315	        ctx: Option<(&[Token], &[Token])>,
   316	        src: &[char],
   317	    ) -> String {
   318	        let fmt = |tokens: &[Token]| {
   319	            tokens
   320	                .iter()
   321	                .filter(|t| !t.kind.is_unlintable())
   322	                .map(|t| t.span.get_content_string(src))
   323	                .collect::<String>()
   324	        };
   325	
   326	        if let Some((pro, epi)) = ctx {
   327	            format!(
   328	                "\x1b[2m{}\x1b[0m{}\x1b[2m{}\x1b[0m",
   329	                fmt(pro),
   330	                fmt(log),
   331	                fmt(epi)
   332	            )
   333	        } else {
   334	            fmt(log)
   335	        }
   336	    }
   337	}
   338	
   339	#[cfg(test)]
   340	pub mod tests {
   341	    use crate::{Document, Span, Token, linting::Linter};
   342	    use hashbrown::HashSet;
   343	
   344	    /// Extension trait for converting spans of tokens back to their original text
   345	    pub trait SpanVecExt {
   346	        fn to_strings(&self, doc: &Document) -> Vec<String>;
   347	    }
   348	
   349	    impl SpanVecExt for Vec<Span<Token>> {
   350	        fn to_strings(&self, doc: &Document) -> Vec<String> {
   351	            self.iter()
   352	                .map(|sp| {
   353	                    doc.get_tokens()[sp.start..sp.end]
   354	                        .iter()
   355	                        .map(|tok| doc.get_span_content_str(&tok.span))
   356	                        .collect::<String>()
   357	                })
   358	                .collect()
   359	        }
   360	    }
   361	
   362	    // Special Linter just for testing
   363	    use crate::{
   364	        CharStringExt, Lint, TokenStringExt,
   365	        linting::{LintKind, Suggestion},
   366	    };
   367	
   368	    /// Type alias for many:many error-to-fix mappings used in testing
   369	    /// Each error pattern can map to multiple possible fixes
   370	    pub type TestLinterMap<'a> = &'a [(&'a [&'a str], &'a [&'a str])];
   371	
   372	    #[derive(Clone)]
   373	    pub struct TestLinter<'a> {
   374	        map: TestLinterMap<'a>,
   375	    }
   376	    impl<'a> TestLinter<'a> {
   377	        pub fn new(map: TestLinterMap<'a>) -> Self {
   378	            Self { map }
   379	        }
   380	    }
   381	    impl<'a> Linter for TestLinter<'a> {
   382	        fn lint(&mut self, doc: &Document) -> Vec<Lint> {
   383	            let mut corr: Vec<(Span<char>, &[char], &[&str])> = Vec::new();
   384	            for wordtok in doc.iter_words() {
   385	                let wordspan = wordtok.span;
   386	                let word_chars = wordspan.get_content(doc.get_source());
   387	                // Check if word matches any of the patterns in the map
   388	                for (errors, fixes) in self.map {
   389	                    // if any of the errors match, add all of the corrections
   390	                    if errors
   391	                        .iter()
   392	                        .any(|&e| word_chars.eq_ignore_ascii_case_str(e))
   393	                    {
   394	                        corr.push((wordspan, word_chars, fixes))
   395	                    }
   396	                }
   397	            }
   398	            corr.iter()
   399	                .map(|(ws, wch, cstr)| {
   400	                    // Create suggestions for all possible fixes
   401	                    let suggestions: Vec<Suggestion> = cstr
   402	                        .iter()
   403	                        .map(|&suggestion_str| {
   404	                            Suggestion::replace_with_match_case(
   405	                                suggestion_str.chars().collect(),
   406	                                wch.to_owned(),
   407	                            )
   408	                        })
   409	                        .collect();
   410	
   411	                    Lint {
   412	                        span: *ws,
   413	                        lint_kind: LintKind::Spelling,
   414	                        suggestions,
   415	                        message: "Test linter for 'linting assertion' tests".to_string(),
   416	                        ..Default::default()
   417	                    }
   418	                })
   419	                .collect()
   420	        }
   421	        fn description(&self) -> &str {
   422	            "Test linter for 'linting assertion' tests"
   423	        }

   470	    pub fn assert_lint_count(text: &str, mut linter: impl Linter, count: usize) {
   471	        let test = Document::new_plain_english_curated(text);
   472	        let lints = linter.lint(&test);
   473	        // dbg!(&lints);
   474	        if lints.len() != count {
   475	            panic!(
   476	                "Expected \"{text}\" to create {count} lints, but it created {}.",
   477	                lints.len()
   478	            );
   479	        }
   480	    }

   500	    /// Assert the total number of suggestions produced by a [`Linter`], spread across all produced
   501	    /// [`Lint`]s.
   502	    #[track_caller]
   503	    pub fn assert_suggestion_count(text: &str, mut linter: impl Linter, count: usize) {
   504	        let test = Document::new_plain_english_curated(text);
   505	        let lints = linter.lint(&test);
   506	        eprintln!(
   507	            "{}",
   508	            lints
   509	                .iter()
   510	                .map(|l| l
   511	                    .suggestions
   512	                    .iter()
   513	                    .map(|s| s.to_string())
   514	                    .collect::<Vec<_>>()
   515	                    .join(", "))
   516	                .collect::<Vec<_>>()
   517	                .join("\n")
   518	        );
   519	        assert_eq!(
   520	            lints.iter().map(|l| l.suggestions.len()).sum::<usize>(),
   521	            count
   522	        );
   523	    }

   554	    /// Applies suggestions iteratively until any combination produces the expected result.
   555	    ///
   556	    /// Explores all possible suggestion branches (depth-first search) until finding a path
   557	    /// that produces the expected result. Stops after 100 iterations to prevent infinite loops.
   558	    ///
   559	    /// Use this when you want to verify that *some* suggestion sequence produces the
   560	    /// expected result, without caring which specific suggestions are used.
   561	    ///
   562	    /// See issue #950: https://github.com/Automattic/harper/issues/950
   563	    #[track_caller]
   564	    pub fn assert_suggestion_result(text: &str, mut linter: impl Linter, needle: &str) {
   565	        if search_for_suggestion(DocumentType::PlainEnglish, text, &mut linter, needle, 0) {
   566	            return;
   567	        }
   568	
   569	        panic!(
   570	            "No suggestion sequence produced the expected result.\n\
   571	            Expected: \"{needle}\""
   572	        );
   573	    }

   254	
   255	fn ser_ordered<S>(map: &HashMap<String, Option<bool>>, ser: S) -> Result<S::Ok, S::Error>
   256	where
   257	    S: Serializer,
   258	{
   259	    let ordered: BTreeMap<_, _> = map.iter().map(|(k, v)| (k.clone(), *v)).collect();
   260	    ordered.serialize(ser)
   261	}
   262	
   263	fn de_hashbrown<'de, D>(de: D) -> Result<HashMap<String, Option<bool>>, D::Error>
   264	where
   265	    D: Deserializer<'de>,
   266	{
   267	    let ordered: BTreeMap<String, Option<bool>> = BTreeMap::deserialize(de)?;
   268	    Ok(ordered.into_iter().collect())
   269	}
   270	
   271	/// The configuration for a [`LintGroup`].
   272	/// Each child linter can be enabled, disabled, or set to a curated value.
   273	#[derive(Debug, Serialize, Deserialize, Default, Clone, PartialEq, Eq)]
   274	#[serde(transparent)]
   275	pub struct LintGroupConfig {
   276	    /// We do this shenanigans with the [`BTreeMap`] to keep the serialized format consistent.
   277	    #[serde(serialize_with = "ser_ordered", deserialize_with = "de_hashbrown")]
   278	    inner: HashMap<String, Option<bool>>,
   279	}
   280	
   281	#[cached]
   282	fn curated_config() -> LintGroupConfig {
   283	    // The Dictionary and Dialect do not matter, we're just after the config.
   284	    let group = LintGroup::new_curated(MutableDictionary::new().into(), Dialect::American);
   285	    group.config
   286	}
   287	
   288	impl LintGroupConfig {
   289	    /// Check if a rule exists in the configuration.
   290	    pub fn has_rule(&self, key: impl AsRef<str>) -> bool {
   291	        self.inner.contains_key(key.as_ref())
   292	    }
   293	
   294	    pub fn set_rule_enabled(&mut self, key: impl ToString, val: bool) {
   295	        self.inner.insert(key.to_string(), Some(val));
   296	    }
   297	
   298	    /// Remove any configuration attached to a rule.
   299	    /// This allows it to assume its default (curated) state.
   300	    pub fn unset_rule_enabled(&mut self, key: impl AsRef<str>) {
   301	        self.inner.remove(key.as_ref());
   302	    }
   303	
   304	    pub fn set_rule_enabled_if_unset(&mut self, key: impl AsRef<str>, val: bool) {
   305	        if !self.inner.contains_key(key.as_ref()) {
   306	            self.set_rule_enabled(key.as_ref().to_string(), val);
   307	        }
   308	    }
   309	
   310	    pub fn is_rule_enabled(&self, key: &str) -> bool {
   311	        self.inner.get(key).cloned().flatten().unwrap_or(false)
   312	    }
   313	
   314	    /// Clear all config options.
   315	    /// This will reset them all to disable them.
   316	    pub fn clear(&mut self) {
   317	        for val in self.inner.values_mut() {
   318	            *val = None
   319	        }
   320	    }
   321	
   322	    /// Merge the contents of another [`LintGroupConfig`] into this one.
   323	    /// The other config will be left empty after this operation.
   324	    ///
   325	    /// Conflicting keys will be overridden by the value in the other group.
   326	    pub fn merge_from(&mut self, other: &mut LintGroupConfig) {
   327	        for (key, val) in other.inner.iter() {
   328	            if val.is_none() {
   329	                continue;
   330	            }
   331	
   332	            self.inner.insert(key.to_string(), *val);
   333	        }
   334	
   335	        other.clear();
   336	    }
   337	
   338	    /// Fill the group with the values for the curated lint group.
   339	    pub fn fill_with_curated(&mut self) {
   340	        let mut temp = Self::new_curated();
   341	        mem::swap(self, &mut temp);
   342	        self.merge_from(&mut temp);
   343	    }
   344	
   345	    pub fn new_curated() -> Self {
   346	        curated_config()
   347	    }
   348	}
   349	
   350	impl Hash for LintGroupConfig {
   351	    fn hash<H: Hasher>(&self, hasher: &mut H) {
   352	        for (key, value) in &self.inner {
   353	            hasher.write(key.as_bytes());
   354	            if let Some(value) = value {
   355	                hasher.write_u8(1);
   356	                hasher.write_u8(*value as u8);
   357	            } else {
   358	                // Do it twice so we fill the same number of bytes as the other branch.
   359	                hasher.write_u8(0);
   360	                hasher.write_u8(0);
   361	            }
   362	        }
   363	    }
   364	}
   365	
   366	/// A struct for collecting the output of a number of individual [Linter]s.
   367	/// Each child can be toggled via the public, mutable `Self::config` object.
   368	pub struct LintGroup {
   369	    pub config: LintGroupConfig,
   370	    /// We use a binary map here so the ordering is stable.
   371	    linters: BTreeMap<String, Box<dyn Linter>>,
   372	    /// We use a binary map here so the ordering is stable.
   373	    chunk_expr_linters: BTreeMap<String, Box<dyn ExprLinter<Unit = Chunk>>>,
   374	    /// Since [`ExprLinter`]s operate on a chunk-basis, we can store a
   375	    /// mapping of `Chunk -> Lint` and only re-run the expr linters
   376	    /// when a chunk changes.
   377	    ///
   378	    /// Since the expr linter results also depend on the config, we hash it and pass it as part
   379	    /// of the key.
   380	    chunk_expr_cache: LruCache<(CharString, u64), BTreeMap<String, Vec<Lint>>>,
   381	    hasher_builder: RandomState,
   382	    clashing_linter_names: Option<Vec<String>>,
   383	}
   384	
   385	impl LintGroup {
   386	    // Constructor methods
   387	
   388	    pub fn empty() -> Self {
   389	        Self {
   390	            config: LintGroupConfig::default(),
   391	            linters: BTreeMap::new(),
   392	            chunk_expr_linters: BTreeMap::new(),
   393	            chunk_expr_cache: LruCache::new(NonZero::new(1000).unwrap()),
   394	            hasher_builder: RandomState::default(),
   395	            clashing_linter_names: None,
   396	        }
   397	    }
   398	
   399	    // Non-constructor methods
   400	
   401	    /// Check if the group already contains a linter with a given name.
   402	    pub fn contains_key(&self, name: impl AsRef<str>) -> bool {
   403	        self.linters.contains_key(name.as_ref())
   404	            || self.chunk_expr_linters.contains_key(name.as_ref())
   405	    }

Here's the result of running `cat -n` on /testbed/harper-core/src/expr/sequence_expr.rs:
     1	use paste::paste;
     2	
     3	use crate::{
     4	    CharStringExt, Lrc, Span, Token, TokenKind,
     5	    expr::{FirstMatchOf, FixedPhrase, LongestMatchOf},
     6	    patterns::{AnyPattern, IndefiniteArticle, WhitespacePattern, Word, WordSet},
     7	};
     8	
     9	use super::{Expr, Optional, OwnedExprExt, Repeating, Step, UnlessStep};
    10	
    11	#[derive(Default)]
    12	pub struct SequenceExpr {
    13	    exprs: Vec<Box<dyn Expr>>,
    14	}
    15	
    16	/// Generate a `then_*` method from an available `is_*` function on [`TokenKind`].
    17	macro_rules! gen_then_from_is {
    18	    ($quality:ident) => {
    19	        paste! {
    20	            #[doc = concat!("Adds a step matching a token where [`TokenKind::is_", stringify!($quality), "()`] returns true.")]
    21	            pub fn [< then_$quality >] (self) -> Self{
    22	                self.then_kind_where(|kind| {
    23	                    kind.[< is_$quality >]()
    24	                })
    25	            }
    26	
    27	            #[doc = concat!("Adds an optional step matching a token where [`TokenKind::is_", stringify!($quality), "()`] returns true.")]
    28	            pub fn [< then_optional_$quality >] (self) -> Self{
    29	                self.then_optional(|tok: &Token, _source: &[char]| {
    30	                    tok.kind.[< is_$quality >]()
    31	                })
    32	            }
    33	
    34	            #[doc = concat!("Adds a step matching one or more consecutive tokens where [`TokenKind::is_", stringify!($quality), "()`] returns true.")]
    35	            pub fn [< then_one_or_more_$quality s >] (self) -> Self{
    36	                self.then_one_or_more(Box::new(|tok: &Token, _source: &[char]| {
    37	                    tok.kind.[< is_$quality >]()
    38	                }))
    39	            }
    40	
    41	            #[doc = concat!("Adds a step matching a token where [`TokenKind::is_", stringify!($quality), "()`] returns false.")]
    42	            pub fn [< then_anything_but_$quality >] (self) -> Self{
    43	                self.then_kind_where(|kind| {
    44	                    !kind.[< is_$quality >]()
    45	                })
    46	            }
    47	        }
    48	    };
    49	}
    50	
    51	impl Expr for SequenceExpr {
    52	    /// Run the expression starting at an index, returning the total matched window.
    53	    ///
    54	    /// If any step returns `None`, the entire expression does as well.
    55	    fn run(&self, mut cursor: usize, tokens: &[Token], source: &[char]) -> Option<Span<Token>> {
    56	        let mut window = Span::empty(cursor);
    57	
    58	        for cur_expr in &self.exprs {
    59	            let out = cur_expr.run(cursor, tokens, source)?;
    60	
    61	            // Only expand the window if the match actually covers some tokens
    62	            if out.end > out.start {
    63	                window.expand_to_include(out.start);
    64	                window.expand_to_include(out.end.checked_sub(1).unwrap_or(out.start));
    65	            }
    66	
    67	            // Only advance cursor if we actually matched something
    68	            if out.end > cursor {
    69	                cursor = out.end;
    70	            } else if out.start < cursor {
    71	                cursor = out.start;
    72	            }
    73	            // If both start and end are equal to cursor, don't move the cursor
    74	        }
    75	
    76	        Some(window)
    77	    }
    78	}
    79	
    80	impl SequenceExpr {
    81	    // Constructor methods
    82	
    83	    // Match an [expression](Expr).
    84	    pub fn with(expr: impl Expr + 'static) -> Self {
    85	        Self::default().then(expr)
    86	    }
    87	
    88	    // Single token methods
    89	
    90	    /// Construct a new sequence with an [`AnyPattern`] at the beginning of the operation list.
    91	    pub fn anything() -> Self {
    92	        Self::default().then_anything()
    93	    }
    94	
    95	    // Single word token methods
    96	
    97	    /// Construct a new sequence with a [`Word`] at the beginning of the operation list.
    98	    pub fn any_capitalization_of(word: &'static str) -> Self {
    99	        Self::default().then_any_capitalization_of(word)
   100	    }
   101	
   102	    /// Shorthand for [`Self::any_capitalization_of`].
   103	    pub fn aco(word: &'static str) -> Self {
   104	        Self::any_capitalization_of(word)
   105	    }
   106	
   107	    /// Match any word from the given set of words, case-insensitive.
   108	    pub fn word_set(words: &'static [&'static str]) -> Self {
   109	        Self::default().then_word_set(words)
   110	    }
   111	
   112	    /// Match any word.
   113	    pub fn any_word() -> Self {
   114	        Self::default().then_any_word()
   115	    }
   116	
   117	    // Expressions of more than one token
   118	
   119	    /// Optionally match an expression.
   120	    pub fn optional(expr: impl Expr + 'static) -> Self {
   121	        Self::default().then_optional(expr)
   122	    }
   123	
   124	    /// Match a fixed phrase.
   125	    pub fn fixed_phrase(phrase: &'static str) -> Self {
   126	        Self::default().then_fixed_phrase(phrase)
   127	    }
   128	
   129	    // Multiple expressions
   130	
   131	    /// Match the first of multiple expressions.
   132	    pub fn any_of(exprs: Vec<Box<dyn Expr>>) -> Self {
   133	        Self::default().then_any_of(exprs)
   134	    }
   135	
   136	    /// Match the longest of multiple expressions.
   137	    pub fn longest_of(exprs: Vec<Box<dyn Expr>>) -> Self {
   138	        Self::default().then_longest_of(exprs)
   139	    }
   140	
   141	    pub fn whitespace() -> Self {
   142	        Self::default().then_whitespace()
   143	    }
   144	
   145	    /// Will be accepted unless the condition matches.
   146	    pub fn unless(condition: impl Expr + 'static) -> Self {
   147	        Self::default().then_unless(condition)
   148	    }
   149	
   150	    // Builder methods
   151	
   152	    /// Push an [expression](Expr) to the operation list.
   153	    pub fn then(mut self, expr: impl Expr + 'static) -> Self {
   154	        self.exprs.push(Box::new(expr));
   155	        self
   156	    }
   157	
   158	    /// Push an already-boxed [expression](Expr) to the operation list.
   159	    pub fn then_boxed(mut self, expr: Box<dyn Expr>) -> Self {
   160	        self.exprs.push(expr);
   161	        self
   162	    }
   163	
   164	    /// Pushes an expression that could move the cursor to the sequence, but does not require it.
   165	    pub fn then_optional(mut self, expr: impl Expr + 'static) -> Self {
   166	        self.exprs.push(Box::new(Optional::new(expr)));
   167	        self
   168	    }
   169	
   170	    /// Pushes an expression that will match any of the provided expressions.
   171	    ///
   172	    /// If more than one of the provided expressions match, this function provides no guarantee
   173	    /// as to which match will end up being used. If you need to get the longest of multiple
   174	    /// matches, use [`Self::then_longest_of()`] instead.
   175	    pub fn then_any_of(mut self, exprs: Vec<Box<dyn Expr>>) -> Self {
   176	        self.exprs.push(Box::new(FirstMatchOf::new(exprs)));
   177	        self
   178	    }
   179	
   180	    /// Pushes an expression that will match the longest of the provided expressions.
   181	    ///
   182	    /// If you don't need the longest match, prefer using the short-circuiting
   183	    /// [`Self::then_any_of()`] instead.
   184	    pub fn then_longest_of(mut self, exprs: Vec<Box<dyn Expr>>) -> Self {
   185	        self.exprs.push(Box::new(LongestMatchOf::new(exprs)));
   186	        self
   187	    }
   188	
   189	    /// Appends the steps in `other` onto the end of `self`.
   190	    /// This is more efficient than [`Self::then`] because it avoids pointer redirection.
   191	    pub fn then_seq(mut self, mut other: Self) -> Self {
   192	        self.exprs.append(&mut other.exprs);
   193	        self
   194	    }
   195	
   196	    /// Pushes an expression that will match any word from the given set of words, case-insensitive.
   197	    pub fn then_word_set(self, words: &'static [&'static str]) -> Self {
   198	        self.then(WordSet::new(words))
   199	    }
   200	
   201	    /// Shorthand for [`Self::then_word_set`].
   202	    pub fn t_set(self, words: &'static [&'static str]) -> Self {
   203	        self.then_word_set(words)
   204	    }
   205	
   206	    /// Match against one or more whitespace tokens.
   207	    pub fn then_whitespace(self) -> Self {
   208	        self.then(WhitespacePattern)
   209	    }
   210	
   211	    /// Shorthand for [`Self::then_whitespace`].
   212	    pub fn t_ws(self) -> Self {
   213	        self.then_whitespace()
   214	    }
   215	
   216	    /// Match against one or more whitespace tokens.
   217	    pub fn then_whitespace_or_hyphen(self) -> Self {
   218	        self.then(WhitespacePattern.or(|tok: &Token, _: &[char]| tok.kind.is_hyphen()))
   219	    }
   220	
   221	    /// Shorthand for [`Self::then_whitespace_or_hyphen`].
   222	    pub fn t_ws_h(self) -> Self {
   223	        self.then_whitespace_or_hyphen()
   224	    }
   225	
   226	    /// Match against zero or more occurrences of the given expression. Like `*` in regex.
   227	    pub fn then_zero_or_more(self, expr: impl Expr + 'static) -> Self {
   228	        self.then(Repeating::new(Box::new(expr), 0))
   229	    }
   230	
   231	    /// Match against one or more occurrences of the given expression. Like `+` in regex.
   232	    pub fn then_one_or_more(self, expr: impl Expr + 'static) -> Self {
   233	        self.then(Repeating::new(Box::new(expr), 1))
   234	    }
   235	
   236	    /// Match against zero or more whitespace-separated occurrences of the given expression.
   237	    pub fn then_zero_or_more_spaced(self, expr: impl Expr + 'static) -> Self {
   238	        let expr = Lrc::new(expr);
   239	        self.then(SequenceExpr::with(expr.clone()).then(Repeating::new(
   240	            Box::new(SequenceExpr::default().t_ws().then(expr)),
   241	            0,
   242	        )))
   243	    }
   244	
   245	    /// Create a new condition that will step one token forward if met.
   246	    /// If the condition is _not_ met, the whole expression returns `None`.
   247	    ///
   248	    /// This can be used to build out exceptions to other rules.
   249	    ///
   250	    /// See [`UnlessStep`] for more info.
   251	    pub fn then_unless(self, condition: impl Expr + 'static) -> Self {
   252	        self.then(UnlessStep::new(condition, |_tok: &Token, _src: &[char]| {
   253	            true
   254	        }))
   255	    }
   256	
   257	    /// Match any single token.
   258	    ///
   259	    /// See [`AnyPattern`] for more info.
   260	    pub fn then_anything(self) -> Self {
   261	        self.then(AnyPattern)
   262	    }
   263	
   264	    /// Match any single token.
   265	    ///
   266	    /// Shorthand for [`Self::then_anything`].
   267	    pub fn t_any(self) -> Self {
   268	        self.then_anything()
   269	    }
   270	
   271	    // Word matching methods
   272	
   273	    /// Matches any word.
   274	    pub fn then_any_word(self) -> Self {
   275	        self.then_kind_where(|kind| kind.is_word())
   276	    }
   277	
   278	    /// Match examples of `word` that have any capitalization.
   279	    pub fn then_any_capitalization_of(self, word: &'static str) -> Self {
   280	        self.then(Word::new(word))
   281	    }
   282	
   283	    /// Shorthand for [`Self::then_any_capitalization_of`].
   284	    pub fn t_aco(self, word: &'static str) -> Self {
   285	        self.then_any_capitalization_of(word)
   286	    }
   287	
   288	    /// Match examples of `word` case-sensitively.
   289	    pub fn then_exact_word(self, word: &'static str) -> Self {
   290	        self.then(Word::new_exact(word))
   291	    }
   292	
   293	    /// Match a fixed phrase.
   294	    pub fn then_fixed_phrase(self, phrase: &'static str) -> Self {
   295	        self.then(FixedPhrase::from_phrase(phrase))
   296	    }
   297	
   298	    /// Match any word except the ones in `words`.
   299	    pub fn then_word_except(self, words: &'static [&'static str]) -> Self {
   300	        self.then(move |tok: &Token, src: &[char]| {
   301	            !tok.kind.is_word()
   302	                || !words
   303	                    .iter()
   304	                    .any(|&word| tok.span.get_content(src).eq_ignore_ascii_case_str(word))
   305	        })
   306	    }
   307	
   308	    // Token kind/predicate matching methods
   309	
   310	    // One kind
   311	
   312	    /// Matches any token whose `Kind` exactly matches.
   313	    pub fn then_kind(self, kind: TokenKind) -> Self {
   314	        self.then_kind_where(move |k| kind == *k)
   315	    }
   316	
   317	    /// Matches a token where the provided closure returns true for the token's kind.
   318	    pub fn then_kind_where<F>(mut self, predicate: F) -> Self
   319	    where
   320	        F: Fn(&TokenKind) -> bool + Send + Sync + 'static,
   321	    {
   322	        self.exprs
   323	            .push(Box::new(move |tok: &Token, _source: &[char]| {
   324	                predicate(&tok.kind)
   325	            }));
   326	        self
   327	    }
   328	
   329	    /// Match a token of a given kind which is not in the list of words.
   330	    pub fn then_kind_except<F>(self, pred_is: F, ex: &'static [&'static str]) -> Self
   331	    where
   332	        F: Fn(&TokenKind) -> bool + Send + Sync + 'static,
   333	    {
   334	        self.then(move |tok: &Token, src: &[char]| {
   335	            pred_is(&tok.kind)
   336	                && !ex
   337	                    .iter()
   338	                    .any(|&word| tok.span.get_content(src).eq_ignore_ascii_case_str(word))
   339	        })
   340	    }
   341	
   342	    // Two kinds
   343	
   344	    /// Match a token where both token kind predicates return true.
   345	    /// For instance, a word that can be both noun and verb.
   346	    pub fn then_kind_both<F1, F2>(self, pred_is_1: F1, pred_is_2: F2) -> Self
   347	    where
   348	        F1: Fn(&TokenKind) -> bool + Send + Sync + 'static,
   349	        F2: Fn(&TokenKind) -> bool + Send + Sync + 'static,
   350	    {
   351	        self.then_kind_where(move |k| pred_is_1(k) && pred_is_2(k))
   352	    }
   353	
   354	    /// Match a token where either of the two token kind predicates returns true.
   355	    /// For instance, an adjective or an adverb.
   356	    pub fn then_kind_either<F1, F2>(self, pred_is_1: F1, pred_is_2: F2) -> Self
   357	    where
   358	        F1: Fn(&TokenKind) -> bool + Send + Sync + 'static,
   359	        F2: Fn(&TokenKind) -> bool + Send + Sync + 'static,
   360	    {
   361	        self.then_kind_where(move |k| pred_is_1(k) || pred_is_2(k))
   362	    }
   363	
   364	    /// Match a token where neither of the two token kind predicates returns true.
   365	    /// For instance, a word that can't be a verb or a noun.
   366	    pub fn then_kind_neither<F1, F2>(self, pred_isnt_1: F1, pred_isnt_2: F2) -> Self
   367	    where
   368	        F1: Fn(&TokenKind) -> bool + Send + Sync + 'static,
   369	        F2: Fn(&TokenKind) -> bool + Send + Sync + 'static,
   370	    {
   371	        self.then_kind_where(move |k| !pred_isnt_1(k) && !pred_isnt_2(k))
   372	    }
   373	
   374	    /// Match a token where the first token kind predicate returns true and the second returns false.
   375	    /// For instance, a word that can be a noun but cannot be a verb.
   376	    pub fn then_kind_is_but_is_not<F1, F2>(self, pred_is: F1, pred_not: F2) -> Self
   377	    where
   378	        F1: Fn(&TokenKind) -> bool + Send + Sync + 'static,
   379	        F2: Fn(&TokenKind) -> bool + Send + Sync + 'static,
   380	    {
   381	        self.then_kind_where(move |k| pred_is(k) && !pred_not(k))
   382	    }
   383	
   384	    /// Match a token where the first token kind predicate returns true and the second returns false,
   385	    /// and the token is not in the list of exceptions.
   386	    pub fn then_kind_is_but_is_not_except<F1, F2>(
   387	        self,
   388	        pred_is: F1,
   389	        pred_not: F2,
   390	        ex: &'static [&'static str],
   391	    ) -> Self
   392	    where

   394	        F2: Fn(&TokenKind) -> bool + Send + Sync + 'static,

   396	        self.then(move |tok: &Token, src: &[char]| {
   397	            pred_is(&tok.kind)
   398	                && !pred_not(&tok.kind)
   399	                && !ex
   400	                    .iter()
   401	                    .any(|&word| tok.span.get_content(src).eq_ignore_ascii_case_str(word))
   402	        })
   403	    }

    55	                .into_iter()
    56	                .map(|p| {
    57	                    let expr: Box<dyn Expr> = Box::new(weir_expr_to_expr(p.as_ref()).unwrap());
    58	                    expr
    59	                })
    60	                .collect(),
    61	        );
    62	
    63	        Self::new(
    64	            Box::new(patterns),
    65	            correct_forms,
    66	            message,
    67	            description,
    68	            lint_kind,
    69	        )
    70	    }
    71	
    72	    pub fn new_fixed_phrase(
    73	        phrase: impl AsRef<str>,
    74	        correct_forms: impl IntoIterator<Item = impl ToString>,
    75	        message: impl ToString,
    76	        description: impl ToString,
    77	        lint_kind: Option<LintKind>,
    78	    ) -> Self {
    79	        Self::new(
    80	            Box::new(FixedPhrase::from_phrase(phrase.as_ref())),
    81	            correct_forms,
    82	            message,
    83	            description,
    84	            lint_kind,
    85	        )
    86	    }
    87	
    88	    pub fn new_closed_compound(phrase: impl AsRef<str>, correct_form: impl ToString) -> Self {
    89	        let message = format!(
    90	            "Did you mean the closed compound `{}`?",
    91	            correct_form.to_string()
    92	        );
    93	
    94	        let description = format!(
    95	            "Looks for incorrect spacing inside the closed compound `{}`.",
    96	            correct_form.to_string()
    97	        );
    98	
    99	        Self::new_fixed_phrase(
   100	            phrase,
   101	            [correct_form],
   102	            message,
   103	            description,
   104	            Some(LintKind::Miscellaneous),
   105	        )
   106	    }
   107	}
   108	
   109	impl ExprLinter for MapPhraseLinter {
   110	    type Unit = Chunk;
   111	
   112	    fn expr(&self) -> &dyn Expr {
   113	        self.expr.as_ref()
   114	    }
   115	
   116	    fn match_to_lint(&self, matched_tokens: &[Token], source: &[char]) -> Option<Lint> {
   117	        let span = matched_tokens.span()?;
   118	        let matched_text = span.get_content(source);
   119	
   120	        Some(Lint {
   121	            span,
   122	            lint_kind: self.lint_kind,
   123	            suggestions: self
   124	                .correct_forms
   125	                .iter()
   126	                .map(|correct_form| {
   127	                    Suggestion::replace_with_match_case(
   128	                        correct_form.chars().collect(),
   129	                        matched_text,
   130	                    )
   131	                })
   132	                .collect(),
   133	            message: self.message.to_string(),
   134	            priority: 31,
   135	        })
   136	    }
   137	
   138	    fn description(&self) -> &str {
   139	        self.description.as_str()
   140	    }
   141	}
   142

    Lint, Token, TokenKind,
    expr::{Expr, SequenceExpr},
    linting::{ExprLinter, LintKind, Suggestion, expr_linter::Chunk},
};

pub struct FlauntFlout {
    expr: SequenceExpr,
}

impl Default for FlauntFlout {
    fn default() -> Self {
        Self {
            expr: SequenceExpr::word_set(&["flaunt", "flaunted", "flaunting", "flaunts"])
                .t_ws()
                .then_word_set(&[
                    "law", "laws", "rule", "rules", "regulation", "regulations",
                    "convention", "conventions", "standard", "standards",
                    "protocol", "protocols", "code", "codes",
                    "norm", "norms", "guideline", "guidelines",
                ]),
        }
    }
}

impl ExprLinter for FlauntFlout {
    type Unit = Chunk;

    fn expr(&self) -> &dyn Expr {
        &self.expr
    }

    fn match_to_lint(&self, toks: &[Token], src: &[char]) -> Option<Lint> {
        let verb_span = toks.first()?.span;
        let verb_chars = verb_span.get_content(src);

        enum Form {
            Base,
            Past,
            Ing,
            ThirdPerson,
        }

        let infl = match verb_chars.last().map(|c| c.to_ascii_lowercase()) {
            Some('"'"'t'"'"') => Form::Base,
            Some('"'"'d'"'"') => Form::Past,
            Some('"'"'g'"'"') => Form::Ing,
            Some('"'"'s'"'"') => Form::ThirdPerson,
            _ => return None,
        };

        Some(Lint {
            span: verb_span,
            lint_kind: LintKind::WordChoice,
            suggestions: vec![Suggestion::replace_with_match_case_str(
                match infl {
                    Form::Base => "flout",
                    Form::Past => "flouted",
                    Form::Ing => "flouting",
                    Form::ThirdPerson => "flouts",
                },
                verb_chars,
            )],
            message: "`Flaunt` means to show off. Did you mean `flout` (to openly disregard)?".to_string(),
            ..Default::default()
        })
    }

    fn description(&self) -> &str {
        "Looks for `flaunt` wrongly used when `flout` (to openly disregard rules) is intended."
    }
}

   565	    pub fn assert_suggestion_result(text: &str, mut linter: impl Linter, needle: &str) {
   566	        if search_for_suggestion(DocumentType::PlainEnglish, text, &mut linter, needle, 0) {
   567	            return;
   568	        }
   569	
   570	        panic!(
   571	            "No suggestion sequence produced the expected result.\n\
   572	            Expected: \"{needle}\""
   573	        );
   574	    }
   575	
   576	    /// DFS implementation using markdown instead of plain English
   577	    #[track_caller]
   578	    pub fn assert_markdown_suggestion_result(text: &str, mut linter: impl Linter, needle: &str) {
   579	        if !search_for_suggestion(DocumentType::Markdown, text, &mut linter, needle, 0) {
   580	            panic!("No suggestion sequence produced the expected result.\nExpected: {needle}");
   581	        }
   582	    }
   583	
   584	    /// Recursively searches all suggestion combinations using depth-first search.
   585	    /// Returns true if any path reaches the expected result, false otherwise.
   586	    fn search_for_suggestion(
   587	        doc_type: DocumentType,
   588	        text: &str,
   589	        linter: &mut impl Linter,
   590	        needle: &str,
   591	        depth: usize,
   592	    ) -> bool {
   593	        // Prevent infinite recursion (e.g. cycles in suggestions)
   594	        if depth > 100 {
   595	            eprintln!("⚠️  Reached depth limit (100)");
   596	            return false;
   597	        }
   598	
   599	        // Check if we've reached the expected result
   600	        if text == needle {
   601	            return true;
   602	        }
   603	
   604	        // Lint current text and try each suggestion branch
   605	        let chars: Vec<char> = text.chars().collect();
   606	        let document = create_document(&chars, doc_type);
   607	        let lints = linter.lint(&document);
   608	
   609	        if let Some(lint) = lints.first() {
   610	            for sug in lint.suggestions.iter() {
   611	                let mut chars_copy = chars.clone();
   612	                sug.apply(lint.span, &mut chars_copy);
   613	                let next: String = chars_copy.iter().collect();
   614	
   615	                // Recursively search this branch
   616	                if search_for_suggestion(doc_type, &next, linter, needle, depth + 1) {
   617	                    return true;
   618	                }
   619	            }
   620	        }

OK. The issue is likely that the linter is not finding a match. Let me debug by adding a test that just checks the lint count:

Let me first add a simpler test to see if the linter matches at all. Let me look at how other similar tests (like `BrandBrandish`) work:

The `BrandBrandish` linter uses:
```rust
expr: SequenceExpr::word_set(&["brandish", "brandished", "brandishes", "brandishing"])
    .t_ws()
    .then_kind_except(TokenKind::is_object_pronoun, &["her", "it", "them"]),
```

This matches "brandish" + whitespace + a token that is NOT an object pronoun (except her/it/them). So it's looking for "brandish him" (where "him" is an object pronoun) and flagging it.

For my flaunt/flout linter, I'm matching:
```rust
expr: SequenceExpr::word_set(&["flaunt", "flaunted", "flaunting", "flaunts"])
    .t_ws()
    .then_word_set(&["law", "laws", "rule", "rules", ...]),
```

This should match "flaunted" + whitespace + "laws", etc.

But wait - there might be intervening words like "the" between "flaunted" and "laws". For example: "flaunted US bankruptcy laws". Here, "US" and "bankruptcy" come between "flaunted" and "laws".

So my expression is too simplistic. I need to handle the case where there are modifying words between the verb and the target noun. Let me look at how other linters handle this...

Actually, looking at the PR description examples more carefully:
- "He **flaunted** US bankruptcy laws for personal gain."
- "It's got a Kirk-esque captain who **flaunts** the rules..."
- "That's what deranged scientists **flaunting** the laws of God and Man are for"
- "some seem to **flaunt** the basic rules of punctuation and grammar."

The target words (laws, rules) are not necessarily the immediate next word. There can be articles, adjectives, etc. in between.

However, looking at the `BrandBrandish` linter, it only looks at the immediately following word (after whitespace). That works for "brandish him" patterns.

For the flaunt/flout case, we need to be smarter. But given the complexity, maybe a simpler approach would work: we could flag ALL uses of "flaunt" and suggest "flout" as an alternative, but that would be too aggressive and cause false positives.

Let me reconsider the approach. Looking at the PR description again, it says:
> "flaunt" is a very common mistake where "flout" is obviously meant

Perhaps the approach should be simpler: just add "flaunt" → "flout" as a spelling/confusion suggestion when it appears with rule/law-related words somewhere nearby. But the `MapPhraseSetLinter` framework is phrase-based, not context-based.

     1	use crate::{Span, Token, expr::Expr};
     2	
     3	/// An [`Expr`] that matches against tokens if and only if all of its children do.
     4	/// This can be useful for situations where you have multiple expressions that represent a grammatical
     5	/// error, but you need _all_ of them to match to be certain.
     6	///
     7	/// It will return the position of the farthest window.
     8	#[derive(Default)]
     9	pub struct All {
    10	    children: Vec<Box<dyn Expr>>,
    11	}
    12	
    13	impl All {
    14	    pub fn new(children: Vec<Box<dyn Expr>>) -> Self {
    15	        Self { children }
    16	    }
    17	
    18	    pub fn add(&mut self, e: impl Expr + 'static) {
    19	        self.children.push(Box::new(e));
    20	    }
    21	}
    22	
    23	impl Expr for All {
    24	    fn run(&self, cursor: usize, tokens: &[Token], source: &[char]) -> Option<Span<Token>> {
    25	        let mut longest: Option<Span<Token>> = None;
    26	
    27	        for expr in self.children.iter() {
    28	            let window = expr.run(cursor, tokens, source)?;
    29	
    30	            if let Some(longest_window) = longest {
    31	                if window.len() > longest_window.len() {
    32	                    longest = Some(window);
    33	                }
    34	            } else {
    35	                longest = Some(window);
    36	            }
    37	        }
    38	
    39	        longest
    40	    }
    41	}

So the linter is not matching at all. The expression doesn't match because of the intervening words. Let me check what the tokenization looks like. For "He flaunted US bankruptcy laws", the tokens are likely:
- "He" (pronoun)
- " " (whitespace)
- "flaunted" (verb)
- " " (whitespace)  
- "US" (word)
- " " (whitespace)
- "bankruptcy" (word)
- " " (whitespace)
- "laws" (noun)

So my expression `WordSet(["flaunted"]) + whitespace + WordSet(["laws"])` wouldn't match because there are "US" and "bankruptcy" between them.

I need to allow zero or more words between the verb and the target noun. Let me look at how to do this with the SequenceExpr API.

Looking at the API, there's `then_zero_or_more` which matches zero or more occurrences of an expression. I could use:
```rust
SequenceExpr::word_set(&["flaunt", ...])
    .t_ws()
    .then_zero_or_more(SequenceExpr::any_word().t_ws())
    .then_word_set(&["law", "laws", ...])
```

But this might be too complex. Let me look at how other linters handle multi-word gaps.

Actually, looking at the `BrandBrandish` example, it only looks at the immediately following word. That's a simpler pattern. For the flaunt/flout case, maybe I should take a simpler approach: just flag "flaunt" whenever it appears before rule/law words, but with the flexibility to have intervening words.

Let me look at how `SequenceExpr` can be used with `then_zero_or_more`:

    35	/// A trait that searches for tokens that fulfil [`Expr`]s in a [`Document`].
    36	///
    37	/// Makes use of [`TokenStringExt::iter_chunks`] by default, or [`TokenStringExt::iter_sentences`] to process either
    38	/// a chunk (clause) or a sentence at a time.
    39	#[blanket(derive(Box))]
    40	pub trait ExprLinter: LSend {
    41	    type Unit: DocumentIterator;
    42	
    43	    /// A simple getter for the expression you want Harper to search for.
    44	    fn expr(&self) -> &dyn Expr;
    45	    /// If any portions of a [`Document`] match [`Self::expr`], they are passed through [`ExprLinter::match_to_lint`]
    46	    /// or [`ExprLinter::match_to_lint_with_context`] to be transformed into a [`Lint`] for editor consumption.
    47	    ///
    48	    /// Transform matched tokens into a [`Lint`] for editor consumption.
    49	    ///
    50	    /// This is the simple version that only sees the matched tokens. For context-aware linting,
    51	    /// implement `match_to_lint_with_context` instead.
    52	    ///
    53	    /// Return `None` to skip producing a lint for this match.
    54	    fn match_to_lint(&self, matched_tokens: &[Token], source: &[char]) -> Option<Lint> {
    55	        self.match_to_lint_with_context(matched_tokens, source, None)
    56	    }
    57	
    58	    /// Transform matched tokens into a [`Lint`] with access to surrounding context.
    59	    ///
    60	    /// The context provides access to tokens before and after the match. When implementing
    61	    /// this method, you can call `self.match_to_lint()` as a fallback if the context isn't needed.
    62	    ///
    63	    /// Return `None` to skip producing a lint for this match.
    64	    fn match_to_lint_with_context(
    65	        &self,
    66	        matched_tokens: &[Token],
    67	        source: &[char],
    68	        _context: Option<(&[Token], &[Token])>,
    69	    ) -> Option<Lint> {
    70	        // Default implementation falls back to the simple version
    71	        self.match_to_lint(matched_tokens, source)
    72	    }
    73	    /// A user-facing description of what kinds of grammatical errors this rule looks for.
    74	    /// It is usually shown in settings menus.
    75	    fn description(&self) -> &str;
    76	}
    77	
    78	/// Helper function to find the only occurrence of a token matching a predicate
    79	///
    80	/// Returns `Some(token)` if exactly one token matches the predicate, `None` otherwise.
    81	/// TODO: This can be used in the [`ThenThan`] linter when #1819 is merged.
    82	pub fn find_the_only_token_matching<'a, F>(
    83	    tokens: &'a [Token],
    84	    source: &[char],
    85	    predicate: F,
    86	) -> Option<&'a Token>
    87	where
    88	    F: Fn(&Token, &[char]) -> bool,
    89	{
    90	    let mut matches = tokens.iter().filter(|&tok| predicate(tok, source));
    91	    match (matches.next(), matches.next()) {
    92	        (Some(tok), None) => Some(tok),
    93	        _ => None,
    94	    }
    95	}

    97	impl<L, U> Linter for L
    98	where
    99	    L: ExprLinter<Unit = U>,
   100	    U: DocumentIterator,
   101	{
   102	    fn lint(&mut self, document: &Document) -> Vec<Lint> {
   103	        let mut lints = Vec::new();
   104	        let source = document.get_source();
   105	
   106	        for unit in U::iter_units(document) {
   107	            lints.extend(run_on_chunk(self, unit, source));
   108	        }
   109	
   110	        lints
   111	    }
   112	
   113	    fn description(&self) -> &str {
   114	        self.description()
   115	    }
   116	}
   117	
   118	pub fn run_on_chunk<'a>(
   119	    linter: &'a impl ExprLinter,
   120	    unit: &'a [Token],
   121	    source: &'a [char],
   122	) -> impl Iterator<Item = Lint> + 'a {
   123	    linter
   124	        .expr()
   125	        .iter_matches(unit, source)
   126	        .filter_map(|match_span| {
   127	            linter.match_to_lint_with_context(
   128	                &unit[match_span.start..match_span.end],
   129	                source,
   130	                Some((&unit[..match_span.start], &unit[match_span.end..])),
   131	            )
   132	        })
   133	}
   134	
   135	/// Check for sentence continuation after a matched span.
   136	///
   137	/// Validates that the "after" context starts with whitespace followed by a word token,
   138	/// allowing flexible inspection of that word's properties (POS tags, etc.) via the predicate.
   139	/// The predicate can be used to confirm matches, suppress false positives, or apply conditional logic.
   140	///
   141	/// Returns `false` if context is `None`, missing tokens, or the structure is malformed.
   142	pub fn followed_by_word(
   143	    context: Option<(&[Token], &[Token])>,
   144	    predicate: impl Fn(&Token) -> bool,
   145	) -> bool {
   146	    if let Some((_, after)) = context
   147	        && let [ws, word, ..] = after
   148	        && ws.kind.is_whitespace()
   149	    {
   150	        return predicate(word);
   151	    }
   152	    false
   153	}
   154	
   155	pub fn preceded_by_word(
   156	    context: Option<(&[Token], &[Token])>,
   157	    predicate: impl Fn(&Token) -> bool,
   158	) -> bool {
   159	    if let Some((before, _)) = context
   160	        && let [.., word, ws] = before
   161	        && ws.kind.is_whitespace()
   162	    {
   163	        return predicate(word);
   164	    }
   165	    false
   166	}

   229	        fn match_to_lint_with_context(
   230	            &self,
   231	            toks: &[Token],
   232	            src: &[char],
   233	            context: Option<(&[Token], &[Token])>,
   234	        ) -> Option<Lint> {
   235	            if let Some((before, after)) = context {
   236	                let before = before.span()?.get_content_string(src);
   237	                let after = after.span()?.get_content_string(src);
   238	
   239	                let (message, suggestions) = if before.eq_ignore_ascii_case("one ")
   240	                    && after.eq_ignore_ascii_case(" three")
   241	                {
   242	                    (
   243	                        "ascending".to_string(),
   244	                        vec![Suggestion::ReplaceWith(vec!['>'])],

   246	                } else if before.eq_ignore_ascii_case("three ")
   247	                    && after.eq_ignore_ascii_case(" one")
   248	                {
   249	                    (
   250	                        "descending".to_string(),

   257	                    )

   259

   261	                    span: toks.span()?,

   110	fn add(u: usize, i: isize) -> Option<usize> {
   111	    if i.is_negative() {
   112	        u.checked_sub(i.wrapping_abs() as u32 as usize)
   113	    } else {
   114	        u.checked_add(i as usize)
   115	    }

   117	
   118	pub trait ExprExt {
   119	    /// Iterate over all matches of this expression in the document, automatically filtering out
   120	    /// overlapping matches, preferring the first.
   121	    fn iter_matches<'a>(
   122	        &'a self,
   123	        tokens: &'a [Token],
   124	        source: &'a [char],
   125	    ) -> Box<dyn Iterator<Item = Span<Token>> + 'a>;
   126	
   127	    fn iter_matches_in_doc<'a>(
   128	        &'a self,
   129	        doc: &'a Document,
   130	    ) -> Box<dyn Iterator<Item = Span<Token>> + 'a>;
   131	}
   132	
   133	impl<E: ?Sized> ExprExt for E
   134	where
   135	    E: Expr,
   136	{
   137	    fn iter_matches<'a>(
   138	        &'a self,
   139	        tokens: &'a [Token],
   140	        source: &'a [char],
   141	    ) -> Box<dyn Iterator<Item = Span<Token>> + 'a> {
   142	        let mut last_end = 0usize;
   143	
   144	        Box::new((0..tokens.len()).filter_map(move |i| {
   145	            let span = self.run(i, tokens, source)?;
   146	            if span.start >= last_end {
   147	                last_end = span.end;
   148	                Some(span)
   149	            } else {
   150	                None
   151	            }
   152	        }))
   153	    }
   154	
   155	    fn iter_matches_in_doc<'a>(
   156	        &'a self,
   157	        doc: &'a Document,
   158	    ) -> Box<dyn Iterator<Item = Span<Token>> + 'a> {
   159	        Box::new(self.iter_matches(doc.get_tokens(), doc.get_source()))
   160	    }
   161	}
   162

     1	use super::Expr;
     2	use crate::{Span, Token};
     3	
     4	/// An expression that will match one or more repetitions of the same expression.
     5	///
     6	/// Somewhat reminiscent of the `+*` operator in Regex.
     7	pub struct Repeating {
     8	    inner: Box<dyn Expr>,
     9	    required_repetitions: usize,
    10	}
    11	
    12	impl Repeating {
    13	    pub fn new(expr: Box<dyn Expr>, required_repetitions: usize) -> Self {
    14	        Self {
    15	            inner: expr,
    16	            required_repetitions,
    17	        }
    18	    }
    19	}
    20	
    21	impl Expr for Repeating {
    22	    fn run(&self, mut cursor: usize, tokens: &[Token], source: &[char]) -> Option<Span<Token>> {
    23	        let mut window = Span::empty(cursor);
    24	        let mut repetition = 0;
    25	
    26	        loop {
    27	            let res = self.inner.run(cursor, tokens, source);
    28	
    29	            if let Some(res) = res {
    30	                window.expand_to_include(res.start);
    31	                window.expand_to_include(res.end - 1);
    32	
    33	                if res.start < cursor {
    34	                    cursor = res.start;
    35	                } else {
    36	                    cursor = res.end;
    37	                }
    38	
    39	                if res.is_empty() {
    40	                    return Some(window);
    41	                }
    42	
    43	                repetition += 1;
    44	            } else if repetition >= self.required_repetitions {
    45	                return Some(window);
    46	            } else {
    47	                return None;
    48	            }
    49	        }
    50	    }
    51	}
    52

I see. The `Repeating` with `required_repetitions: 0` will match zero or more times. But there's a subtlety: when the inner expression is `SequenceExpr::any_word().t_ws()`, it expects a word then whitespace. But after the last word before "laws", there might not be whitespace after it (since "laws" is the target, not followed by whitespace in the pattern). Actually, the pattern is:

```
flaunt -> ws -> (any_word -> ws)* -> laws
```

So "laws" would be matched by the final `then_word_set`. But the zero-or-more group expects `any_word + whitespace`. For "flaunted US bankruptcy laws":
- "flaunted" matches first word set
- ws matches
- "US" matches any_word, then ws matches
- "bankruptcy" matches any_word, then ws matches
- "laws" should match the final word set. 

But wait, after "bankruptcy" there's whitespace, then "laws". So the zero-or-more group should match "US" + ws + "bankruptcy" + ws. Then the final `then_word_set` should match "laws".

That should work. Let me check if there's an issue with `SequenceExpr` inside `Repeating`. Let me look at how `SequenceExpr` handles `from(AnyPattern)`:

     9	impl Default for BestOfAllTime {
    10	    fn default() -> Self {
    11	        // Best, Biggest
    12	        let inflection_superlative = SequenceExpr::default().then_superlative_adjective();
    13	        // Most interesting
    14	        let most_superlative = SequenceExpr::default()
    15	            .t_aco("most")
    16	            .t_ws()
    17	            .then_positive_adjective();

    19	        let fave_or_top = SequenceExpr::word_set(&["favorite", "favourite", "top"]);
    20	
    21	        // We can't use the noun phrase Expr because it allows determiners before the nouns and "best the thing" wouldn't be right
    22	        let expr = SequenceExpr::any_of(vec![
    23	            Box::new(inflection_superlative),
    24	            Box::new(most_superlative),
    25	            Box::new(fave_or_top),
    26	        ])
    27	        // There is no non-greedy `Repeating` in Harper, so we have to do match non-noun-oov tokens
    28	        // rather than matching arbitrary tokens.
    29	        // We include OOV because novel words not in the dictionary tend to be nouns.
    30	        .then_zero_or_more(|tok: &Token, _: &[char]| !tok.kind.is_noun() && !tok.kind.is_oov())

Interesting! In `best_of_all_time.rs`, line 30:
```rust
.then_zero_or_more(|tok: &Token, _: &[char]| !tok.kind.is_noun() && !tok.kind.is_oov())
```

This uses a closure directly, not a `SequenceExpr`. Note that `then_zero_or_more` can take a closure. But when I call `.then_zero_or_more(SequenceExpr::any_word().t_ws())`, I'm passing a `SequenceExpr`, which implements `Expr`. That should work.

But wait - let me check the `then_zero_or_more` signature again:

```rust
pub fn then_zero_or_more(self, expr: impl Expr + 'static) -> Self {
    self.then(Repeating::new(Box::new(expr), 0))
}
```

So it takes an `Expr`. `SequenceExpr::any_word().t_ws()` is a `SequenceExpr` which implements `Expr`. So this should work.

But the issue might be that the `Repeating` expression doesn't stop at the right place. It will greedily match as many `any_word + ws` as possible, and then try to match the final `then_word_set`. If it matches all words including the target word (like "laws"), then the final `then_word_set` would fail because there's nothing left to match.

Wait, `Repeating` is greedy but it tries to match the inner expression. If the inner expression is `any_word + ws`, it would match "US" + ws, then "bankruptcy" + ws, then "laws" + ws. But after "laws" there might not be whitespace (or there might be, if it's followed by "for"). So it would match "laws" + ws too, consuming "laws". Then the final `then_word_set` would have nothing left to match.

That's the problem! The zero-or-more pattern is greedy and consumes the target word too.

I need a different approach. Let me use a non-greedy approach like in `best_of_all_time.rs` where they use:
```rust
.then_zero_or_more(|tok: &Token, _: &[char]| !tok.kind.is_noun() && !tok.kind.is_oov())
```

This matches tokens that are NOT nouns and NOT OOV (out-of-vocabulary). So it matches everything except nouns, then the final noun is matched by `.then_kind_where(|kind| kind.is_noun() || kind.is_oov())`.

For my case, I want to match "flaunt" + (any non-rule/law words) + (rule/law words). Let me adapt this pattern:

pub struct FlauntFlout {
    expr: SequenceExpr,
}

impl Default for FlauntFlout {
    fn default() -> Self {
        // Match "flaunt" (and inflected forms) followed by words related to rules/laws,
        // with optional intervening non-rule/law words.
        let rule_words = &[
            "law", "laws", "rule", "rules", "regulation", "regulations",
            "convention", "conventions", "standard", "standards",
            "protocol", "protocols", "code", "codes",
            "norm", "norms", "guideline", "guidelines",
        ];

        Self {
            expr: SequenceExpr::word_set(&["flaunt", "flaunted", "flaunting", "flaunts"])
                .t_ws()
                .then_zero_or_more(|tok: &Token, src: &[char]| {
                    if tok.kind.is_word() {
                        let word = tok.span.get_content_string(src).to_lowercase();
                        !rule_words.contains(&word.as_str())
                    } else {
                        !tok.kind.is_word()
                    }
                })
                .then_word_set(rule_words),
        }
    }
}'

Wait, this still won't work correctly because the zero-or-more matches ANY token (including whitespace) that isn't a rule word. But the `Repeating` will keep consuming tokens greedily. The problem is that the final `then_word_set` won't match because the zero-or-more already consumed everything.

Actually, let me re-think. The `Repeating` tries the inner expression repeatedly. Each iteration, it tries the inner expression. If the inner expression succeeds, it consumes those tokens. If it fails, it stops (since `required_repetitions` is 0, it can stop at zero matches).

So for "flaunted US bankruptcy laws for personal gain":
- "flaunted" matches first word set
- ws (after "flaunted") matches `t_ws()`
- Now the zero-or-more tries: `|tok: &Token, src: &[char]| { ... }` which matches "US" (not a rule word), then whitespace, then "bankruptcy" (not a rule word), then whitespace, then "laws"... wait, "laws" IS a rule word! So the closure returns `false` for "laws" (because `!rule_words.contains(&word.as_str())` is false), so it stops. Then the final `then_word_set(rule_words)` matches "laws".

That should work! Let me run the tests:

     9	}
    10	
    11	impl Default for FlauntFlout {
    12	    fn default() -> Self {
    13	        // Match "flaunt" (and inflected forms) followed by words related to rules/laws,
    14	        // with optional intervening non-rule/law words.
    15	        let rule_words = &[
    16	            "law", "laws", "rule", "rules", "regulation", "regulations",
    17	            "convention", "conventions", "standard", "standards",
    18	            "protocol", "protocols", "code", "codes",

    20	        ];

    24	                .t_ws()
    25	                .then_zero_or_more(|tok: &Token, src: &[char]| {
    26	                    if tok.kind.is_word() {
    27	                        let word = tok.span.get_content_string(src).to_lowercase();
    28	                        !rule_words.contains(&word.as_str())

The implementation looks good. Let me also think about some additional edge cases:

1. **"flaunt the law"** - "law" is a rule word, so this would be flagged. But what if someone means "show off the law"? That seems unlikely; "flout the law" is the common phrase.

2. **"flaunt convention"** - "convention" is in the list. "flout convention" is indeed the correct phrase when meaning to openly ignore convention.

3. **"flaunt protocol"** - Similar situation.

4. **Capitalization**: The `WordSet` matches case-insensitively, and `get_content_string` returns the original text. The suggestion uses `replace_with_match_case_str` which should preserve the original capitalization pattern.

5. **Punctuation after the target word**: In "He flaunted the rules.", after "rules" there's a period. The final `then_word_set` matches "rules" (it doesn't care what comes after). That's correct.

Let me test a few more edge cases by adding some quick tests:

Actually, let me also think about the `then_zero_or_more` closure. The `else` branch returns `!tok.kind.is_word()`. For non-word tokens (whitespace, punctuation), this returns `true`, meaning they will be consumed by the zero-or-more loop. But we need whitespace to be consumed because there's whitespace between words. And punctuation between words would also be consumed.

But there's a subtle issue: after the zero-or-more loop consumes punctuation like "." or ",", the final `then_word_set` would try to match the next token, which might not exist or might be something else entirely. However, since the zero-or-more stops when it encounters a rule word (because the closure returns `false` for rule words), and rule words are words, this should be fine.

Wait, there's another issue: what if the zero-or-more encounters a period? For example: "He flaunted. The law was clear." Here, the zero-or-more would match "." (not a word, so `!tok.kind.is_word()` returns `true`), then whitespace, then "The" (not a rule word), then whitespace, then "law" (is a rule word, stops). Then `then_word_set` matches "law". But this would be a false positive because "He flaunted." is a complete sentence, not related to "law". However, this is unlikely because the sentence structure would be unusual.

Let me also consider if I should limit how many tokens the zero-or-more can match. In `best_of_all_time.rs`, they limit to non-noun and non-OOV tokens. But for my case, I want to allow any words except rule words.

I think the current implementation is reasonable. Let me add a few more edge case tests:
